					<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading mw-first-heading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Entrepreneurship</span></h1>

<div class="hlist"><ul><li><span class="nowrap"><span class="noviewer" typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Emblem-money.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Emblem-money.svg/20px-Emblem-money.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Emblem-money.svg/40px-Emblem-money.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></a></span> </span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Economics" title="Portal:Economics">Economics&#32;portal</a></li><li><span class="nowrap"><span class="skin-invert-image noviewer" typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Social_sciences.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Social_sciences.svg/20px-Social_sciences.svg.png" decoding="async" width="17" height="15" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Social_sciences.svg/40px-Social_sciences.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="139" data-file-height="122" /></a></span> </span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Society" title="Portal:Society">Society&#32;portal</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1333133064" /><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1239400231" /><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Economics_sidebar" title="Template:Economics sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Economics_sidebar" title="Template talk:Economics sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Template:Economics_sidebar" title="Special:EditPage/Template:Economics sidebar"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Entrepreneurship</b> is the creation or extraction of <a href="/wiki/Economic_value" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic value">economic value</a> by identifying and <a href="/wiki/Commercialization" title="Commercialization">commercializing</a> opportunities to deliver <a href="/wiki/Goods_and_services" title="Goods and services">products or services</a>, a process that typically requires considerable initiative and bears risk.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This process may also encompass the pursuit of values that extend beyond mere economic considerations.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2025)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The term <b>entrepreneur</b> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">French:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="fr-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">&#91;ɑ̃tʁəpʁənœʁ&#93;</a></span>) refers to an <a href="/wiki/Businessperson" title="Businessperson">individual</a> who creates and/or invests in one or more <a href="/wiki/Company" title="Company">businesses</a>, bearing most of the risks and enjoying most of the rewards.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:4&#95;2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The process of setting up a business is also referred to as "entrepreneurship".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2025)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The entrepreneur is often regarded as an <a href="/wiki/Innovator" class="mw-redirect" title="Innovator">innovator</a>, a source of new <a href="/wiki/Business_idea" title="Business idea">ideas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goods" title="Goods">goods</a>, services, and business procedures.
</p><p>Narrower definitions of entrepreneurship include the process of designing, launching, and operating a new business, often similar to a <a href="/wiki/Small_business" title="Small business">small business</a>, or (per <i>Business Dictionary</i>) as the "capacity and willingness to develop, organize, and manage a business venture along with any of its risks to make a <a href="/wiki/Profit_(accounting)" title="Profit (accounting)">profit</a>".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-businessdictionary.com&#95;3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-businessdictionary.com-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Individuals who create these businesses are often referred to as "entrepreneurs".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-moves&#95;5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moves-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="Quotation needed from source to verify. (October 2025)">need quotation to verify</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In the field of economics, the term <i>entrepreneur</i> is used for an entity that has the ability to translate <a href="/wiki/Invention" title="Invention">inventions</a> or <a href="/wiki/Technologies" class="mw-redirect" title="Technologies">technologies</a> into products and services.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In this sense, entrepreneurship encompasses the activities of both established firms and startups.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Perspectives_on_entrepreneurship">Perspectives on entrepreneurship</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entrepreneurship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Perspectives on entrepreneurship"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In the 21st century, the governments of <a href="/wiki/Nation_state" title="Nation state">nation states</a> have tried to promote entrepreneurship, as well as <a href="/wiki/Business" title="Business">enterprise culture</a>, in the hope that it would improve or stimulate economic growth and <a href="/wiki/Competition_(economics)" title="Competition (economics)">competition</a>. After the end of <a href="/wiki/Supply-side_economics" title="Supply-side economics">supply-side economics</a>, entrepreneurship was supposed to boost the economy.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>As an academic field, entrepreneurship accommodates different schools of thought. It has been studied within disciplines such as <a href="/wiki/Management" title="Management">management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">economics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sociology" title="Sociology">sociology</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Economic_history" title="Economic history">economic history</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some view entrepreneurship as allocated to <i>the entrepreneur</i>. These scholars tend to focus on <a href="#Elements">what the entrepreneur does</a> and what traits an entrepreneur has. This is sometimes referred to as the functionalistic approach to entrepreneurship.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-auto&#95;10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Others deviate from the individualistic perspective to turn the spotlight on <i>the entrepreneurial process</i> and immerse in the interplay between agency and context. This approach is sometimes referred to as the processual approach,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-auto&#95;10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> or the contextual turn/approach to entrepreneurship.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-auto1&#95;12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Elements">Elements</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entrepreneurship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Elements"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>

.ambox{margin:0 10%}}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .ambox{display:none!important}}</style><table class="box-More&#95;citations&#95;needed&#95;section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span <p>Entrepreneurship includes the creation or extraction of <a href="/wiki/Economic_value" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic value">economic value</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-auto1&#95;12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is the act of being an entrepreneur, or the owner or manager of a business enterprise who, by risk and initiative, attempts to make profits.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:4&#95;2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Entrepreneurs act as managers and oversee the launch and growth of an enterprise. According to the scholar V. Ratten, entrepreneurship is defined as:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1244412712">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 32px}.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;margin-top:0}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{padding-left:1.6em}}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>the identification of <a href="/wiki/Business_opportunity" title="Business opportunity">business-related opportunities</a> through a process of using existing, new or a recombination of resources in an innovative and creative way.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>In the early 19th century, the French economist <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Say" title="Jean-Baptiste Say">Jean-Baptiste Say</a> provided a broad definition of entrepreneurship, saying that it "shifts economic resources out of an area of lower and into an area of higher productivity and greater yield". Entrepreneurs create something new and unique—they change or transmute value.
</p><p>Regardless of the firm size, big or small, it can take part in entrepreneurship opportunities. There are four criteria for becoming an entrepreneur. First, there must be opportunities or situations to recombine resources to generate profit. Second, entrepreneurship requires differences between people, such as preferential access to certain individuals or the ability to recognize information about opportunities. Third, taking on a level of risk is a necessity. Fourth, the entrepreneurial process requires the organization of people and resources.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Shane&#95;16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shane-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>An entrepreneur uses their time, energy, and resources to create value for others. They are rewarded for this effort monetarily and therefore both the consumer of the value created and the entrepreneur benefit.
</p><p>The entrepreneur is a factor in and the study of entrepreneurship reaches back to the work of <a href="/wiki/Richard_Cantillon" title="Richard Cantillon">Richard Cantillon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adam_Smith" title="Adam Smith">Adam Smith</a> in the late 17th and early 18th centuries. However, entrepreneurship was largely ignored theoretically until the late 19th and early 20th centuries and empirically until a profound resurgence in business and economics since the late 1970s.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the 20th century, the understanding of entrepreneurship owes much to the work of economist <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Schumpeter" title="Joseph Schumpeter">Joseph Schumpeter</a> in the 1930s and other Austrian economists such as <a href="/wiki/Carl_Menger" title="Carl Menger">Carl Menger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_von_Mises" title="Ludwig von Mises">Ludwig von Mises</a> and <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_von_Hayek" class="mw-redirect" title="Friedrich von Hayek">Friedrich von Hayek</a>. According to Schumpeter, an entrepreneur is a person who is willing and able to convert a new idea or invention into a successful <a href="/wiki/Innovation" title="Innovation">innovation</a>. Entrepreneurship employs what Schumpeter called "the gale of creative destruction" to replace in whole or in part inferior innovations across markets and industries, simultaneously creating new products, including new <a href="/wiki/Business_model" title="Business model">business models</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Extensions of Schumpeter's thesis about entrepreneurship have sought to describe the traits of an entrepreneur using various data sets and techniques. Looking at data from the Global Entrepreneurship Monitor (GEM), entrepreneurial traits specific to the Association of Southeast Asian Nations (ASEAN) are: experience in managing or owning a business, pursuit of an opportunity while being employed, and self-employment. In the decision to establish a new business, the ASEAN entrepreneur depends especially on their own long-term mental model of their enterprise, while scanning for new opportunities in the short-term. These driving characteristics allude to the presence of serial entrepreneurship in the region.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>It has been argued, that <a href="/wiki/Creative_destruction" title="Creative destruction">creative destruction</a> is largely responsible for the dynamism of industries and long-run economic growth. The supposition that entrepreneurship leads to economic growth is an interpretation of the residual in endogenous growth theory and as such is debated in academic economics. An alternative description posited by <a href="/wiki/Israel_Kirzner" title="Israel Kirzner">Israel Kirzner</a> suggests that the majority of innovations may be much more incremental improvements such as the replacement of paper with plastic in the making of <a href="/wiki/Drinking_straw" title="Drinking straw">drinking straws</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Entrepreneurial_opportunities">Entrepreneurial opportunities</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entrepreneurship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Entrepreneurial opportunities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The exploitation of entrepreneurial opportunities may include:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Developing a <a href="/wiki/Business_plan" title="Business plan">business plan</a></li>
<li>Hiring <a href="/wiki/Human_resources" title="Human resources">human resources</a></li>
<li>Acquiring financial and material resources</li>
<li>Providing <a href="/wiki/Leadership" title="Leadership">leadership</a></li>
<li>Being responsible for both the venture's success or failure</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Risk_aversion" title="Risk aversion">Risk aversion</a></li></ul>
<p>The economist <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Schumpeter" title="Joseph Schumpeter">Joseph Schumpeter</a> (1883–1950) saw the role of the entrepreneur in the economy as "<a href="/wiki/Creative_destruction" title="Creative destruction">creative destruction</a>", Which he defined as launching innovations that simultaneously destroy old industries while ushering in new industries and approaches. For Schumpeter, the changes and "dynamic <a href="/wiki/Economic_equilibrium" title="Economic equilibrium">economic equilibrium</a> brought on by the innovating entrepreneur [were] the norm of a healthy economy".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> While entrepreneurship is often associated with new, small, for-profit start-ups, entrepreneurial behavior can be seen in small-, medium- and large-sized firms, new and established firms and in for-profit and not-for-profit organizations, including voluntary-sector groups, charitable organizations and <a href="/wiki/Civil_service" title="Civil service">government</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Entrepreneurship may operate within an <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurship_ecosystem" title="Entrepreneurship ecosystem">entrepreneurship ecosystem</a> which often includes:
</p>
<ul><li>Government programs and services that promote entrepreneurship and support entrepreneurs and start-ups</li>
<li>Non-governmental organizations such as small-business associations and organizations that offer advice and mentoring to entrepreneurs (e.g. through entrepreneurship centers or websites)</li>
<li>Small-business <a href="/wiki/Advocacy_organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Advocacy organization">advocacy organizations</a> that lobby governments for increased support for entrepreneurship programs and more small business-friendly laws and regulations</li>
<li>Entrepreneurship resources and facilities (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Business_incubator" title="Business incubator">business incubators</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seed_accelerator" class="mw-redirect" title="Seed accelerator">seed accelerators</a>)</li>
<li>Entrepreneurship education and training programs offered by schools, colleges and universities</li>
<li>Financing (e.g. bank loans, <a href="/wiki/Venture_capital_financing" class="mw-redirect" title="Venture capital financing">venture capital financing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angel_investing" class="mw-redirect" title="Angel investing">angel investing</a> and government and private foundation grants)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-VentureCapitalNY1&#95;23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VentureCapitalNY1-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="Quotation needed from source to verify. (July 2017)">need quotation to verify</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li></ul>
<p>In the 2000s, usage of the term "entrepreneurship" expanded to include how and why some individuals (or teams) identify opportunities, evaluate them as viable, and then decide to exploit them.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The term has also been used to discuss how people might use these opportunities to develop new products or services, launch new firms or industries, and create wealth.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The entrepreneurial process is uncertain because opportunities can only be identified after they have been exploited.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Entrepreneurs exhibit positive <a href="/wiki/Biases" class="mw-redirect" title="Biases">biases</a> towards finding new possibilities and seeing unmet market needs, and a tendency towards risk-taking that makes them more likely to exploit <a href="/wiki/Business_opportunity" title="Business opportunity">business opportunities</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Zhang&#95;Cueto&#95;Study&#95;of&#95;Bias&#95;in&#95;Entrepreneurship&#95;27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zhang_Cueto_Study_of_Bias_in_Entrepreneurship-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entrepreneurship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Historical_usage">Historical usage</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entrepreneurship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Historical usage"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Wimbit-Jellinek-Phoenix8hp.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Wimbit-Jellinek-Phoenix8hp.jpg/250px-Wimbit-Jellinek-Phoenix8hp.jpg" decoding="async" width="230" height="106" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Wimbit-Jellinek-Phoenix8hp.jpg/500px-Wimbit-Jellinek-Phoenix8hp.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="715" data-file-height="330" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Emil_Jellinek" title="Emil Jellinek">Emil Jellinek-Mercedes</a> (1853–1918), here at the steering wheel of his Phoenix Double-Phaeton</figcaption></figure>
<p>"Entrepreneur" (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/ɒ̃/: nasal &#39;an&#39; in &#39;vin blanc&#39;">ɒ̃</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;p&#39; in &#39;pie&#39;">p</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/ɜːr/: &#39;ur&#39; in &#39;fur&#39;">ɜːr</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span>-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/nj/: &#39;n&#39; in &#39;new&#39;">nj</span><span title="/ʊər/: &#39;our&#39; in &#39;tour&#39;">ʊər</span></span>/</a></span>&#32;<span class="ext-phonos"><span data-nosnippet="" id="ooui-php-1" class="noexcerpt ext-phonos-PhonosButton ext-phonos-PhonosButton-emptylabel oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-buttonElement oo-ui-buttonElement-frameless oo-ui-iconElement oo-ui-buttonWidget" data-ooui="{&quot;_&quot;:&quot;mw.Phonos.PhonosButton&quot;,&quot;href&quot;:&quot;\/\/upload.wikimedia.org\/wikipedia\/commons\/transcoded\/0\/03\/En-us-entrepreneur.ogg\/En-us-entrepreneur.ogg.mp3&quot;,&quot;rel&quot;:[&quot;nofollow&quot;],&quot;framed&quot;:false,&quot;icon&quot;:&quot;volumeUp&quot;,&quot;data&quot;:{&quot;ipa&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;text&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;lang&quot;:&quot;en&quot;,&quot;wikibase&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;file&quot;:&quot;En-us-entrepreneur.ogg&quot;},&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;noexcerpt&quot;,&quot;ext-phonos-PhonosButton&quot;,&quot;ext-phonos-PhonosButton-emptylabel&quot;]}"><a role="button" tabindex="0" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/0/03/En-us-entrepreneur.ogg/En-us-entrepreneur.ogg.mp3" rel="nofollow" aria-label="Play audio" title="Play audio" class="oo-ui-buttonElement-button"><span class="oo-ui-iconElement-icon oo-ui-icon-volumeUp"></span><span class="oo-ui-labelElement-label"></span><span class="oo-ui-indicatorElement-indicator oo-ui-indicatorElement-noIndicator"></span></a></span><sup class="ext-phonos-attribution noexcerpt navigation-not-searchable"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-entrepreneur.ogg" title="File:En-us-entrepreneur.ogg">ⓘ</a></sup></span></span>, <span style="font-size: 85%;">UK also</span> <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;p&#39; in &#39;pie&#39;">p</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/ɛ/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">ɛ</span></span>-/</a></span></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">loanword</a> from French. The word first appeared in the French dictionary entitled <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr">Dictionnaire Universel de Commerce</i></span> compiled by Jacques des Bruslons and published in 1723.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Especially in Britain, the term "adventurer" was often used to denote the same meaning.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The study of entrepreneurship reaches back to the work in the late 17th and early 18th centuries of Irish-French economist <a href="/wiki/Richard_Cantillon" title="Richard Cantillon">Richard Cantillon</a>, which was foundational to <a href="/wiki/Classical_economics" title="Classical economics">classical economics</a>. Cantillon defined the term first in his <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr">Essai sur la Nature du Commerce en Général</i></span>, or <i>Essay on the Nature of Trade in General</i>, a book <a href="/wiki/William_Stanley_Jevons" title="William Stanley Jevons">William Stanley Jevons</a> considered the "cradle of political economy".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Cantillon defined the term as a person who pays a certain price for a product and resells it at an uncertain price, "making decisions about obtaining and using the resources while consequently admitting the risk of enterprise". Cantillon considered the entrepreneur to be a risk taker who deliberately allocates resources to exploit opportunities to maximize the financial return.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Cantillon,&#95;R.&#95;1931&#95;33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cantillon,_R._1931-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Cantillon emphasized the willingness of the entrepreneur to assume the risk and to deal with uncertainty, thus he drew attention to the function of the entrepreneur and distinguished between the function of the entrepreneur and the owner who provided the money.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Cantillon,&#95;R.&#95;1931&#95;33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cantillon,_R._1931-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Landström,&#95;H.&#95;2005&#95;35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Landström,_H._2005-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Jean-Baptiste Say also identified entrepreneurs as a driver for economic development, emphasizing their role as one of the collecting factors of production allocating resources from less to fields that are more productive. Both Say and Cantillon belonged to French school of thought and known as the physiocrats.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Dating back to the time of the medieval <a href="/wiki/Guilds" class="mw-redirect" title="Guilds">guilds</a> in Germany, a <a href="/wiki/Craftspeople" class="mw-redirect" title="Craftspeople">craftsperson</a> required special permission to operate as an entrepreneur, the small proof of competence (<span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Kleiner Befähigungsnachweis</i></span>), which restricted training of apprentices to craftspeople who held a <a href="/wiki/Meister" title="Meister">Meister</a> certificate. This institution was introduced in 1908 after a period of so-called freedom of trade (<span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Gewerbefreiheit</i></span>, introduced in 1871) in the <a href="/wiki/German_Reich" title="German Reich">German Reich</a>. However, proof of competence was not required to start a business. In 1935 and in 1953, greater proof of competence was reintroduced (<span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Großer Befähigungsnachweis Kuhlenbeck</i></span>), which required craftspeople to obtain a Meister apprentice-training certificate before being permitted to set up a new business.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Ashanti Empire">Ashanti Empire</a>, successful entrepreneurs who accumulated large wealth and men as well as distinguished themselves through heroic deeds were awarded social and political recognition by being called "Abirempon" which means big men. By the eighteenth and nineteenth centuries AD, the appellation "Abirempon" had formalized and politicized to embrace those who conducted trade from which the whole state benefited. The state rewarded entrepreneurs who attained such accomplishments with Mena(elephant tail) which was the "heraldic badge"<sup id="cite&#95;ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="20th_century">20th century</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entrepreneurship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 20th century"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In the 20th century, entrepreneurship was studied by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Schumpeter" title="Joseph Schumpeter">Joseph Schumpeter</a> in the 1930s and by other <a href="/wiki/Austrian_school" class="mw-redirect" title="Austrian school">Austrian economists</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Carl_Menger" title="Carl Menger">Carl Menger</a> (1840–1921), <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_von_Mises" title="Ludwig von Mises">Ludwig von Mises</a> (1881–1973) and <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_von_Hayek" class="mw-redirect" title="Friedrich von Hayek">Friedrich von Hayek</a> (1899–1992). While the loan from French of the English-language word "entrepreneur" dates to 1762,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the word "entrepreneurism" dates from 1902<sup id="cite&#95;ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the term "entrepreneurship" also first appeared in 1902.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to Schumpeter, an entrepreneur is willing and able to convert a new idea or <a href="/wiki/Invention" title="Invention">invention</a> into a successful <a href="/wiki/Innovation" title="Innovation">innovation</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Schumpeter1976&#95;42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schumpeter1976-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Entrepreneurship employs what Schumpeter called the "gale of <a href="/wiki/Creative_destruction" title="Creative destruction">creative destruction</a>"<sup id="cite&#95;ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
to replace in whole or in part inferior offerings across markets and industries, simultaneously creating new products and new <a href="/wiki/Business_model" title="Business model">business models</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> thus creative destruction is largely<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="This term requires quantification. (September 2020)">quantify</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> responsible for long-term economic growth. The idea that entrepreneurship leads to economic growth is an interpretation of the residual in <a href="/wiki/Endogenous_growth_theory" title="Endogenous growth theory">endogenous growth theory</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (October 2013)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and as such continues to be debated in academic economics. An alternative description by <a href="/wiki/Israel_Kirzner" title="Israel Kirzner">Israel Kirzner</a> (born 1930) suggests that the majority of innovations may be <a href="/wiki/Incrementalism" title="Incrementalism">incremental</a> improvements – such as the replacement of paper with plastic in the construction of a drinking straw – that require no special qualities.
</p><p>For Schumpeter, entrepreneurship resulted in new industries and in new combinations of currently existing inputs. Schumpeter's initial example of this was the combination of a steam engine and then current wagon-making technologies to produce the <a href="/wiki/Horseless_carriage" title="Horseless carriage">horseless carriage</a>. In this case, the innovation (i.e. the car) was <a href="/wiki/Transformation_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Transformation (disambiguation)">transformational</a> but did not require the development of dramatic new technology. It did not immediately replace the horse-drawn carriage, but in time incremental improvements reduced the cost and improved the technology, leading to the modern <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry" title="Automotive industry">auto industry</a>. Despite Schumpeter's early 20th-century contributions, traditional <a href="/wiki/Microeconomic" class="mw-redirect" title="Microeconomic">microeconomic</a> theory did not formally consider the entrepreneur in its theoretical frameworks (instead of assuming that resources would find each other through a price system). In this treatment, the entrepreneur was an implied but unspecified actor, consistent with the concept of the entrepreneur being the agent of <a href="/wiki/X-efficiency" class="mw-redirect" title="X-efficiency">x-efficiency</a>.
</p><p>For Schumpeter, the entrepreneur did not bear <a href="/wiki/Risk" title="Risk">risk</a>: the capitalist did. Schumpeter believed that the equilibrium was imperfect. Schumpeter (1934) demonstrated that the changing environment continuously provides new information about the optimum allocation of resources to enhance profitability. Some individuals acquire the new information before others and recombine the resources to gain an entrepreneurial <a href="/wiki/Profit_(economics)" title="Profit (economics)">profit</a>. Schumpeter was of the opinion that entrepreneurs shift the <a href="/wiki/Production%E2%80%93possibility_frontier" title="Production–possibility frontier">production-possibility curve</a> to a higher level using innovations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Schumpeter1934&#95;44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schumpeter1934-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Initially, <a href="/wiki/Economists" class="mw-redirect" title="Economists">economists</a> made the first attempt<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (September 2020)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> to study the entrepreneurship concept in depth.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Landstrom2007&#95;45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Landstrom2007-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Alfred Marshall viewed the entrepreneur as a multi-tasking capitalist and observed that in the equilibrium of a completely competitive market there was no spot for "entrepreneurs" as economic-activity creators.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Changes in politics and society in Russia and China in the late 20th century saw a flowering of entrepreneurial activity, producing <a href="/wiki/Russian_oligarch" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian oligarch">Russian oligarchs</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_millionaires" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese millionaires">Chinese millionaires</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="21st_century">21st century</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entrepreneurship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 21st century"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ambassador_Verveer_Greets_African_Womens_Entrepreneurship_Program_Participants.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Ambassador_Verveer_Greets_African_Womens_Entrepreneurship_Program_Participants.jpg/250px-Ambassador_Verveer_Greets_African_Womens_Entrepreneurship_Program_Participants.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Ambassador_Verveer_Greets_African_Womens_Entrepreneurship_Program_Participants.jpg/500px-Ambassador_Verveer_Greets_African_Womens_Entrepreneurship_Program_Participants.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a><figcaption>In 2012, Ambassador-at-Large for Global Women's Issues <a href="/wiki/Melanne_Verveer" title="Melanne Verveer">Melanne Verveer</a> greets participants in an African Women's Entrepreneurship Program at the <a href="/wiki/State_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="State Department">State Department</a> in Washington, D.C.</figcaption></figure>
<p>In the 2000s, entrepreneurship was extended from its origins in for-profit businesses to include <a href="/wiki/Social_entrepreneurship" title="Social entrepreneurship">social entrepreneurship</a>, in which business goals are sought alongside social, environmental or humanitarian goals and even the concept of the <a href="/wiki/Political_entrepreneur" title="Political entrepreneur">political entrepreneur</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (August 2013)">according to whom?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Entrepreneurship within an existing firm or large organization has been referred to as <a href="/wiki/Intrapreneurship" title="Intrapreneurship">intrapreneurship</a> and may include corporate ventures where large entities "spin-off" subsidiary organizations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Entrepreneurs are leaders willing to take risk and exercise initiative, taking advantage of market opportunities by planning, organizing and deploying resources,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEDeakinsFreel2009&#95;50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeakinsFreel2009-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> often by innovating to create new or improving existing products or services.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the 2000s, the term "entrepreneurship" has been extended to include a specific <a href="/wiki/Mindset" title="Mindset">mindset</a> resulting in entrepreneurial initiatives, e.g. in the form of <a href="/wiki/Social_entrepreneurship" title="Social entrepreneurship">social entrepreneurship</a>, <a href="/wiki/Political_entrepreneur" title="Political entrepreneur">political entrepreneurship</a> or <a href="/wiki/Knowledge_entrepreneurship" title="Knowledge entrepreneurship">knowledge entrepreneurship</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>According to Paul Reynolds, founder of the <a href="/wiki/Global_Entrepreneurship_Monitor" title="Global Entrepreneurship Monitor">Global Entrepreneurship Monitor</a>, "by the time they reach their retirement years, half of all working men in the United States probably have a period of self-employment of one or more years; one in four may have engaged in self-employment for six or more years. Participating in a new business creation is a common activity among U.S. workers over the course of their careers".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In recent years, entrepreneurship has been claimed as a major driver of economic growth in both the United States and Western Europe.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Entrepreneurial activities differ substantially depending on the type of organization and creativity involved. Entrepreneurship ranges in scale from solo, part-time projects to large-scale undertakings that involve a team and which may create many jobs. Many "high value" entrepreneurial ventures seek <a href="/wiki/Venture_capital" title="Venture capital">venture capital</a> or <a href="/wiki/Angel_investor" title="Angel investor">angel funding</a> (<a href="/wiki/Seed_money" title="Seed money">seed money</a>) to raise <a href="/wiki/Capital_(economics)" title="Capital (economics)">capital</a> for building and expanding the business.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many organizations exist to support would-be entrepreneurs, including specialized government agencies, <a href="/wiki/Business_incubator" title="Business incubator">business incubators</a> (which may be for-profit, non-profit, or operated by a college or university), <a href="/wiki/Science_park" title="Science park">science parks</a> and non-governmental organizations, which include a range of organizations including not-for-profits, charities, foundations and business advocacy groups (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_commerce" title="Chamber of commerce">Chambers of commerce</a>). Beginning in 2008, an annual "Global Entrepreneurship Week" event aimed at "exposing people to the benefits of entrepreneurship" and getting them to "participate in entrepreneurial-related activities" was launched.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (October 2013)">who?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Relationship_between_small_business_and_entrepreneurship">Relationship between small business and entrepreneurship</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entrepreneurship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Relationship between small business and entrepreneurship"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The term "entrepreneur" is often conflated with the term "<a href="/wiki/Small_business" title="Small business">small business</a>" or used interchangeably with this term. While most entrepreneurial ventures start out as a small business, not all small businesses are entrepreneurial in the strict sense of the term. Many small businesses are sole proprietor operations consisting solely of the owner—or they have a small number of employees—and many of these small businesses offer an existing product, process or service and they do not aim at growth. In contrast, entrepreneurial ventures offer an innovative product, process or service and the entrepreneur typically aims to scale up the company by adding employees, seeking international sales and so on, a process which is financed by <a href="/wiki/Venture_capital" title="Venture capital">venture capital</a> and <a href="/wiki/Angel_investor" title="Angel investor">angel investments</a>. In this way, the term "entrepreneur" may be more closely associated with the term "startup". <a href="/wiki/Success_(concept)" class="mw-redirect" title="Success (concept)">Successful</a> entrepreneurs have the ability to lead a business in a positive direction by proper planning, to adapt to changing environments and understand their own strengths and weaknesses.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Historians'_assessment_and_ranking"><span id="Historians.27_assessment_and_ranking"></span>Historians' assessment and ranking</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entrepreneurship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Historians&#039; assessment and ranking"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Meeting the demands of the consumer revolution that helped drive the Industrial Revolution in Great Britain, <a href="/wiki/Josiah_Wedgwood" title="Josiah Wedgwood">Josiah Wedgwood</a>, the 18th-century potter and entrepreneur and pioneer of modern marketing, which includes devising <a href="/wiki/Direct_marketing" title="Direct marketing">direct mail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Money_back_guarantee" class="mw-redirect" title="Money back guarantee">money back guarantees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Door-to-door" title="Door-to-door">travelling salesmen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buy_one,_get_one_free" title="Buy one, get one free">"buy one get one free"</a>, was named by the historian <a href="/wiki/Judith_Flanders" title="Judith Flanders">Judith Flanders</a> as "among the greatest and most innovative retailers the world has ever seen".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Another historian <a href="/wiki/Tristram_Hunt" title="Tristram Hunt">Tristram Hunt</a> called Wedgwood a "difficult, brilliant, creative entrepreneur whose personal drive and extraordinary gifts changed the way we work and live."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Victorian-era Welsh entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Pryce_Pryce-Jones" title="Pryce Pryce-Jones">Pryce Pryce-Jones</a>, who would capitalise on the railway network created during the Industrial Revolution and the modern postal system that also developed in the UK, formed the first <a href="/wiki/Mail_order" title="Mail order">mail order</a> business, with the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> summing up his legacy as "The mail order pioneer who started a billion-pound industry".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A 2002 survey of 58 business history professors gave the top spots in American business history to <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford" title="Henry Ford">Henry Ford</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gates" title="Bill Gates">Bill Gates</a>; <a href="/wiki/John_D._Rockefeller" title="John D. Rockefeller">John D. Rockefeller</a>; <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Carnegie" title="Andrew Carnegie">Andrew Carnegie</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">Thomas Edison</a>. They were followed by <a href="/wiki/Sam_Walton" title="Sam Walton">Sam Walton</a>; <a href="/wiki/J._P._Morgan" title="J. P. Morgan">J. P. Morgan</a>; <a href="/wiki/Alfred_P._Sloan" title="Alfred P. Sloan">Alfred P. Sloan</a>; <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney" title="Walt Disney">Walt Disney</a>; <a href="/wiki/Ray_Kroc" title="Ray Kroc">Ray Kroc</a>; <a href="/wiki/Thomas_J._Watson" title="Thomas J. Watson">Thomas J. Watson</a>; <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Graham_Bell" title="Alexander Graham Bell">Alexander Graham Bell</a>; <a href="/wiki/Eli_Whitney" title="Eli Whitney">Eli Whitney</a>; <a href="/wiki/James_J._Hill" title="James J. Hill">James J. Hill</a>; <a href="/wiki/Jack_Welch" title="Jack Welch">Jack Welch</a>; <a href="/wiki/Cyrus_McCormick" title="Cyrus McCormick">Cyrus McCormick</a>; <a href="/wiki/David_Packard" title="David Packard">David Packard</a>; <a href="/wiki/Bill_Hewlett" title="Bill Hewlett">Bill Hewlett</a>; <a href="/wiki/Cornelius_Vanderbilt" title="Cornelius Vanderbilt">Cornelius Vanderbilt</a>; and <a href="/wiki/George_Westinghouse" title="George Westinghouse">George Westinghouse</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A 1977 survey of management scholars reported the top five pioneers in management ideas were: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Winslow_Taylor" title="Frederick Winslow Taylor">Frederick Winslow Taylor</a>; <a href="/wiki/Chester_Barnard" title="Chester Barnard">Chester Barnard</a>; <a href="/wiki/Frank_Bunker_Gilbreth_Sr." class="mw-redirect" title="Frank Bunker Gilbreth Sr.">Frank Bunker Gilbreth Sr.</a>; <a href="/wiki/Elton_Mayo" title="Elton Mayo">Elton Mayo</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Lillian_Moller_Gilbreth" title="Lillian Moller Gilbreth">Lillian Moller Gilbreth</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Types_of_entrepreneurship">Types of entrepreneurship</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entrepreneurship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Types of entrepreneurship"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Cultural">Cultural</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entrepreneurship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Cultural"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>According to Christopher Rea and Nicolai Volland, cultural entrepreneurship is "practices of individual and collective agency characterized by mobility between cultural professions and modes of cultural production", which refers to creative industry activities and sectors. In their book <i>The Business of Culture</i> (2015), Rea and Volland identify three types of <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">cultural</a> entrepreneur: "cultural personalities", defined as "individuals who buil[d] their own personal brand of creativity as a cultural authority and leverage it to create and sustain various cultural enterprises"; "tycoons", defined as "entrepreneurs who buil[d] substantial clout in the cultural sphere by forging synergies between their industrial, cultural, political, and philanthropic interests"; and "collective enterprises", organizations which may engage in cultural production for profit or not-for-profit purposes.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the 2000s, story-telling has emerged as a field of study in cultural entrepreneurship. Some have argued that entrepreneurs should be considered "skilled cultural operators"<sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> that use stories to build legitimacy, and seize market opportunities and new capital.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Others have concluded that we need to speak of a 'narrative turn' in cultural entrepreneurship research.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Ethnic">Ethnic</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entrepreneurship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Ethnic"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Sir_JACK_COHEN_1898-1979_Entrepreneur_Founder_of_Tesco_Stores_lived_here_as_a_child.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Sir_JACK_COHEN_1898-1979_Entrepreneur_Founder_of_Tesco_Stores_lived_here_as_a_child.jpg/330px-Sir_JACK_COHEN_1898-1979_Entrepreneur_Founder_of_Tesco_Stores_lived_here_as_a_child.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="373" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Sir_JACK_COHEN_1898-1979_Entrepreneur_Founder_of_Tesco_Stores_lived_here_as_a_child.jpg/500px-Sir_JACK_COHEN_1898-1979_Entrepreneur_Founder_of_Tesco_Stores_lived_here_as_a_child.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Sir_JACK_COHEN_1898-1979_Entrepreneur_Founder_of_Tesco_Stores_lived_here_as_a_child.jpg/960px-Sir_JACK_COHEN_1898-1979_Entrepreneur_Founder_of_Tesco_Stores_lived_here_as_a_child.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="4000" /></a><figcaption>Plaque in London commemorating Jewish entrepreneur Sir <a href="/wiki/Jack_Cohen_(businessman)" title="Jack Cohen (businessman)">Jack Cohen</a> who in 1919 founded <a href="/wiki/Tesco" title="Tesco">Tesco</a>, the largest supermarket chain in the UK.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The term "ethnic entrepreneurship" refers to <a href="/wiki/Self-employment" title="Self-employment">self-employed</a> business owners who belong to racial or <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_minority" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic minority">ethnic minority</a> groups in Europe and North America.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Ethnic&#95;67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnic-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A long tradition of academic research explores the experiences and strategies of ethnic entrepreneurs as they strive to integrate economically into mainstream U.S. or European society. Classic cases include 
Jewish merchants and tradespeople in both regions, South Asians in the UK, Koreans, Japanese, and Chinese in the U.S. and the Turks and North Africans in France.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Ethnic&#95;67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnic-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Fish_and_chip" class="mw-redirect" title="Fish and chip">fish and chip</a> industry in the UK was initiated by Jewish entrepreneurs, with Joseph Malin opening the first fish and chip shop in London in the 1860s, while Samuel Isaacs opened the first sit-down fish restaurant in 1896 which he expanded into a chain comprising 22 restaurants.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1882, Jewish brothers Ralph and Albert Slazenger founded <a href="/wiki/Slazenger" title="Slazenger">Slazenger</a>, one of the world's oldest sport brands, which has the longest-running sporting sponsorship in providing tennis balls to <a href="/wiki/Wimbledon_Championships" title="Wimbledon Championships">Wimbledon</a> since 1902.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the 2010s, ethnic entrepreneurship has been studied in the case of Cuban business owners in Miami, Indian motel owners of the U.S. and Chinese business owners in <a href="/wiki/Chinatown" title="Chinatown">Chinatowns</a> across the U.S. While entrepreneurship offers these groups many opportunities for economic advancement, self-employment and business ownership in the U.S. remain unevenly distributed along racial/ethnic lines.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Chaudhary&#95;318–354&#95;73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chaudhary_318–354-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Despite numerous success stories of Asian entrepreneurs, a recent statistical analysis of U.S. census data shows that whites are more likely than Asians, African-Americans and Latinos to be self-employed in high prestige, lucrative industries.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Chaudhary&#95;318–354&#95;73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chaudhary_318–354-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Religious">Religious</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entrepreneurship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Religious"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Religious entrepreneurship refers to both the use of entrepreneurship to pursue religious ends as well as how religion impacts entrepreneurial pursuits. While religion is a central topic in society, it is largely overlooked in entrepreneurship research.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The inclusion of religion may transform entrepreneurship including a focus on opportunities other than profit as well as practices, processes and purpose of entrepreneurship.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Gümüsay suggests a three pillars model to explain religious entrepreneurship: The pillars are the entrepreneurial, socio-economic/ethical, and religio-spiritual in the pursuit of value, values, and the <a href="/wiki/Metaphysical" class="mw-redirect" title="Metaphysical">metaphysical</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Feminist">Feminist</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entrepreneurship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Feminist"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Feminist" class="mw-redirect" title="Feminist">feminist</a> entrepreneur is an individual who applies feminist values and approaches through entrepreneurship, with the goal of improving the quality of life and well-being of girls and women.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many are doing so by creating "for women, by women" enterprises. Feminist entrepreneurs are motivated to enter commercial markets by desire to create wealth and social change, based on the ethics of cooperation, equality and mutual respect.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These endeavours can have the effect of both empowerment and emancipation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Institutional">Institutional</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entrepreneurship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Institutional"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The American-born British economist <a href="/wiki/Edith_Penrose" title="Edith Penrose">Edith Penrose</a> has highlighted the collective nature of entrepreneurship. She mentions that in modern organizations, human resources need to be combined to better capture and create business opportunities.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The sociologist <a href="/wiki/Paul_DiMaggio" title="Paul DiMaggio">Paul DiMaggio</a> (1988:14) has expanded this view to say that "new institutions arise when organized actors with sufficient resources [institutional entrepreneurs] see in them an opportunity to realize interests that they value highly".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The notion has been widely applied.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Millennial">Millennial</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entrepreneurship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Millennial"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The term "millennial entrepreneur" refers to a business owner who is affiliated with <a href="/wiki/Millennials" title="Millennials">millennials</a> (also known as Generation Y), those people born from approximately 1981 to 1996.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Rauch&#95;88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rauch-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The offspring of <a href="/wiki/Baby_boomers" title="Baby boomers">baby boomers</a> and early <a href="/wiki/Generation_X" title="Generation X">Gen Xers</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Strauss&#95;2000&#95;54&#95;89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Strauss_2000_54-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> this generation was brought up using digital technology and mass media. Millennial business owners are well-equipped with knowledge of new technology and new business models and have a strong grasp of its business applications. There have been many breakthrough businesses that have come from millennial entrepreneurs, such as <a href="/wiki/Mark_Zuckerberg" title="Mark Zuckerberg">Mark Zuckerberg</a>, who created Facebook.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, millennials are less likely to engage in entrepreneurship than prior generations. Some of the barriers to entry for entrepreneurs are the economy, debt from schooling, and the challenges of regulatory compliance.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Nascent">Nascent</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entrepreneurship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Nascent"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>A nascent entrepreneur is someone in the process of establishing a business venture.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In this observation, the nascent entrepreneur can be seen as pursuing an <a href="/wiki/Business_opportunity" title="Business opportunity">opportunity</a>, i.e. a possibility to introduce new services or products, serve new markets, or develop more efficient production methods in a profitable manner.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> But before such a venture is actually established, the opportunity is just a venture idea.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In other words, the pursued opportunity is perceptual in nature, propped by the nascent entrepreneur's personal beliefs about the feasibility of the venturing outcomes the nascent entrepreneur seeks to achieve.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Its prescience and value cannot be confirmed ex ante but only gradually, in the context of the actions that the nascent entrepreneur undertakes towards establishing the venture as described in <a href="/wiki/Saras_Sarasvathy" title="Saras Sarasvathy">Saras Sarasvathy</a>'s theory of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Effectuation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Effectuation (page does not exist)">Effectuation</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Ultimately, these actions can lead to a path that the nascent entrepreneur deems no longer attractive or feasible, or result in the emergence of a (viable) business. In this sense, over time, the nascent venture can move towards being discontinued or towards emerging successfully as an operating entity.
</p><p>The distinction between the novice, serial and portfolio entrepreneurs is an example of behavior-based categorization.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other examples are the (related) studies by,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> on start-up event sequences.  Nascent entrepreneurship that emphasizes the series of activities involved in new venture emergence,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Delmar,&#95;F&#95;2004&#95;103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Delmar,_F_2004-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Lichtenstein,&#95;B.&#95;B.&#95;2007&#95;105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lichtenstein,_B._B._2007-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> rather than the solitary act of exploiting an opportunity. Such research will help separate entrepreneurial action into its basic sub-activities and elucidate the inter-relationships between activities, between an activity (or sequence of activities) and an individual's motivation to form an opportunity belief, and between an activity (or sequence of activities) and the knowledge needed to form an opportunity belief. With this research, scholars will be able to begin constructing a theory of the micro-foundations of entrepreneurial action.
</p><p>Scholars interested in nascent entrepreneurship tend to focus less on the single act of opportunity exploitation and more on the series of actions in new venture emergence,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Delmar,&#95;F&#95;2004&#95;103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Delmar,_F_2004-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Lichtenstein,&#95;B.&#95;B.&#95;2007&#95;105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lichtenstein,_B._B._2007-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Indeed, nascent entrepreneurs undertake numerous <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurial" class="mw-redirect" title="Entrepreneurial">entrepreneurial</a> activities, including actions that make their businesses more concrete to themselves and others. For instance, nascent entrepreneurs often look for and purchase facilities and equipment; seek and obtain financial backing, form <a href="/wiki/Legal_entities" class="mw-redirect" title="Legal entities">legal entities</a>, organize teams; and dedicate all their time and energy to their business<sup id="cite&#95;ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Project-based">Project-based</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entrepreneurship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Project-based"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Project entrepreneurs are individuals who are engaged in the repeated assembly or creation of temporary organizations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Ferriani2009&#95;108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferriani2009-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These are organizations that have limited lifespans which are devoted to producing a singular objective or goal and get disbanded rapidly when the project ends. Industries where project-based enterprises are widespread include: <a href="/wiki/Sound_recording" class="mw-redirect" title="Sound recording">sound recording</a>, film production, <a href="/wiki/Software_development" title="Software development">software development</a>, television production, <a href="/wiki/New_media" title="New media">new media</a> and construction.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Faulkner1987&#95;109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Faulkner1987-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> What makes project-entrepreneurs distinctive from a theoretical standpoint is that they have to "rewire" these temporary ventures and modify them to suit the needs of new project opportunities that emerge. A project entrepreneur who used a certain approach and team for one project may have to modify the business model or team for a subsequent project.
</p><p>Project entrepreneurs are exposed repeatedly to problems and tasks typical of the entrepreneurial process.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-DeFillippi2004&#95;110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeFillippi2004-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Indeed, project-based entrepreneurs face two critical challenges that invariably characterize the creation of a new venture: locating the right opportunity to launch the project venture and assembling the most appropriate team to exploit that opportunity. Resolving the first challenge requires project-entrepreneurs to access an extensive range of information needed to seize new investment opportunities. Resolving the second challenge requires assembling a collaborative team that has to fit well with the particular challenges of the project and has to function almost immediately to reduce the risk that performance might be adversely affected.
